Each migration transforms dashboards from one schema version to the next, allowing older dashboards to work with newer Grafana versions.\n    39→\n    40→## Current Schema Versions\n    41→\n    42→- **Minimum Version**: 13\n    43→- **Latest Version**: 42\n    44→- **Backend Location**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/`\n    45→- **Frontend Location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\n    46→\n    47→## Creating a New Migration\n    48→\n    49→### Step 1: Create the Migration File\n    50→\n    51→Create a new file: `v{N}.go` where `{N}` is the target schema version.\n    52→\n    53→```go\n    54→package schemaversion\n    55→\n    56→import \"context\"\n    57→\n    58→// V{N} migrates [describe what this migration does].\n    59→//\n    60→// [Detailed description of the migration including:]\n    61→// - What properties are being changed\n    62→// - Why the migration is necessary\n    63→// - Any special handling or edge cases\n    64→//\n    65→// Example before migration:\n    66→//\n    67→//\t\"panels\": [\n    68→//\t  {\n    69→//\t    \"id\": 1,\n    70→//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n    71→//\t    \"oldProperty\": \"value\"\n    72→//\t  }\n    73→//\t]\n    74→//\n    75→// Example after migration:\n    76→//\n    77→//\t\"panels\": [\n    78→//\t  {\n    79→//\t    \"id\": 1,\n    80→//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n    81→//\t    \"newProperty\": \"value\"\n    82→//\t  }\n    83→//\t]\n    84→func V{N}(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {\n    85→\tdashboard[\"schemaVersion\"] = {N}\n    86→\n    87→\t// Your migration logic here\n    88→\t// Transform dashboard properties as needed\n    89→\n    90→\treturn nil\n    91→}\n    92→```\n    93→\n    94→### Step 2: Register the Migration\n    95→\n    96→Add your migration to `migrations.go`:\n    97→\n    98→```go\n    99→func GetMigrations(dsInfoProvider DataSourceInfoProvider) map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc {\n   100→\treturn map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc{\n   101→\t\t// ... existing migrations\n   102→\t\t{N}: V{N},  // Add your migration here\n   103→\t\t// ... version `{N-1}` with scenarios to cover the specific migration:\n   112→\n   113→```json\n   114→{\n   115→  \"title\": \"V{N} Migration Test Dashboard\",\n   116→  \"schemaVersion\": {N-1},\n   117→ Tests\n   132→\n   133→```bash\n   134→# Run migration tests\n   135→go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\n   136→\n   137→# Run specific migration test\n   138→go test testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n   142→\n   143→### Step 5: Frontend-Backend Consistency Validation\n   144→\n   145→Implement different changes in the migration until frontend matches exactly with the backend side. Add as many scenarios as possible to ensure comprehensive coverage of all use cases.\n   146→\n   147→For detailed testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n   148→\n   149→#### Test Scenarios to Cover\n   150→\n   151→**Panel-Level Changes:**\n   152→- Panels with different types (graph, table, stat, etc.)\n   153→- Panels with nested panels (rows)\n   154→- Panels with various property combinations\n   155→- Panels with missing or null properties\n   156→- Panels with deprecated properties\n   157→\n   158→**Dashboard-Level Changes:**\n   159→- Dashboard properties (title, tags, time, etc.)\n   160→- Templating variables (query, textbox, custom, etc.)\n   161→- Annotations and links\n   162→- Time picker settings\n   163→- Refresh settings\n   164→\n   165→**Edge Cases:**\n   166→- Empty dashboards\n   167→- Dashboards with only rows\n   168→- Dashboards with mixed panel types\n   169→- Dashboards with complex nested structures\n   170→- Dashboards with invalid or malformed data\n   171→\n   172→**Property Transformations:**\n   173→- Property renaming scenarios\n   174→- Property type conversions\n   175→- Property value transformations\n   176→- Property removal scenarios\n   177→- Property addition scenarios\n   178→\n   179→#### Validation Process\n   180→\n   181→1. **Create comprehensive test data** covering all scenarios\n   182→2. **Run backend migration** and capture output\n   183→3. **Run frontend migration** and capture output\n   184→4. **Compare outputs** using strict equality checks\n   185→5. **Iterate on migration logic** until outputs match exactly\n   186→6. **Add more test cases** for any discrepancies found\n   187→\n   188→#### Test Data Requirements\n   189→\n   190→Create multiple test files for each migration:\n   191→- `v{N}.basic.{name}.json` - Basic functionality\n   192→- `v{N}.edge_cases.{name}.json` - Edge cases and error conditions\n   193→- `v{N}.complex.{name}.json` - Complex dashboard structures\n   194→- `v{N}.property_changes.{name}.json` - Property transformation scenarios\n   195→\n   196→### Step 6: Unit Testing\n   197→\n   198→Add comprehensive unit tests for both backend and frontend migrations This includes:\n    24→\n    25→- Changes in one part of the system that could cause other components to fail\n    26→- Deprecations or removal of a feature\n    27→- Changes to an API that could break automation\n    28→- Changes that affect some plugins or functions of Grafana\n    29→- Migrations that can’t be rolled back\n    30→\n    31→For each change, the provided information:\n    32→\n    33→- Helps you determine if you’re affected\n    34→- Describes the change or relevant background information\n    35→- Guides you in how to mitigate for the change or migrate\n    36→- Provides more learning resources\n    37→\n    38→For release highlights and deprecations, refer to our [v10.3 What’s new](https://grafana.com/docs/grafana/<GRAFANA_VERSION>/whatsnew/whats-new-in-v10-3/). Issue [#77569](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/issues/77569).\n    50→\n    51→If you use the Table visualization, you might see some inconsistencies in your panels. We have updated the table column naming. This will potentially affect field transformations and/or field overrides. To resolve this, either:\n    52→\n    53→- Update the transformation you are using\n    54→- Update field override. Issue [#76899](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/issues/76899).\n    55→\n    56→Users who have transformations with the Time field might see their transformations are not working. Those panels that have broken transformations will fail to render. This is because we changed the field key. See related PR: [#69865](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/pull/69865). To resolve this, either:\n    57→\n    58→- Remove the affected panel and re-create it\n    59→- Select the Time field again\n    60→- Edit the time field as Time for transformation in panel.json or dashboard.json. Issue [#76641](https://github.com/grafana/grafana/issues/76641).\n    61→\n    62→### Data source permissions\\*\n    63→\n    64→The following data source permission endpoints have been removed:\n    65→\n    66→- `GET /datasources/:datasourceId/permissions`\n    67→- `POST /api/datasources/:datasourceId/permissions`\n    68→- `DELETE /datasources/:datasourceId/permissions`\n    69→- `POST /datasources/:datasourceId/enable-permissions`\n    70→- `POST /datasources/:datasourceId/disable-permissions`\n    71→\n    72→Please use the following endpoints instead:\n    73→\n    74→- `GET /api/access-control/datasources/:uid` for listing data source permissions\n    75→- `POST /api/access-control/datasources/:uid/users/:id`, `POST /api/access-control/datasources/:uid/teams/:id`, and `POST /api/access-control/datasources/:uid/buildInRoles/:id` for adding or removing data source permissions\n    76→\n    77→If you are using the Grafana provider for Terraform to manage data source permissions, you will need to upgrade your provider to [version 2.6.0](https://registry.terraform.io/providers/grafana/grafana/2.6.0/docs) or newer to ensure that data source permission provisioning keeps working. Issue [#5880](https://github.com/grafana/grafana-enterprise/pull/5880).\n    78→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. If a dashboard doesn't have an explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` object, the migration **skips it entirely**\n3. For dashboards with explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`, the migration works fine\n\nThe problem is:\n- In the backend: If `defaults[\"custom\"]` doesn't exist (type assertion fails with !ok), the code continues to the next panel without initializing the custom object\n- In the frontend: It uses optional chaining (`?.`) to safely access, but if the object doesn't exist, it just skips the 248→\n   249→// processNewFormatMapping handles mappings that are already in the new format\n   250→func processNewFormatMapping(mappingMap map[string]interface{}, valueMaps map[string]interface{}, newMappings *[]interface{}, hasValueMappings bool) bool {\n   251→\tmappingType := mappingMap[\"type\"].(string)\n   252→\tif mappingType == \"value\" {\n   253→\t\t// Consolidate existing value Now I see the critical issue. Looking at the test cases, **ALL test cases have explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`** (see line 24, 38, 52, etc.). There is NO test case for a dashboard that:\n1. Has `fieldConfig` but\n2. Does NOT have `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` explicitly set\n\nThis is the missing test case that would reveal the regression. The regression happens when:1. A dashboard is imported that has `fieldConfig` but no `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` (which is common for older dashboards)\n2. The v38 migration checks if `custom` exists (line 120 of v38.go: `custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})`)\n3. If `custom` doesn't exist, the type assertion fails (ok == false), and the function continues to the next panel\n4. This skips the entire migration for that panel, leaving `displayMode` in place instead of migrating to `cellOptions`\n\nThe problem is that the migration assumes the `custom` object already exists, This causes field override configuration to be silently skipped during both backend and frontend migration, resulting in loss of column formatting (cell display modes, widths, alignment).\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### Primary Issue: Broken Conditional Logic in V38 Migration\n\n**Backend v38 Migration** (`/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`, lines 115-137):\n\n```go\ndefaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // <-- CRITICAL: Entire panel migration skipped if custom doesn't exist\n}\n\n// Migrate displayMode to cellOptions\nif displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n    if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {\n        custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n    }\n    delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n}\n\n// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // <-- Never reached if custom doesn't exist\n```\n\nThe type assertion on line 120 (`custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})`) assumes `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` already exists. When it doesn't:\n- The assertion fails (ok == false)\n- The migration skips to the next panel via `continue` (line 122)\n- **Field overrides are never migrated** because `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` (line 135) is never called\n\n**Frontend v38 Migration** (`/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`, lines 644-674):\n\n```typescript\nif (oldVersion < 38 && finalTargetVersion >= 38) {\n  panelUpgrades.push((panel: PanelModel) => {\n    if (panel.type === 'table' && panel.fieldConfig !== undefined) {\n      const displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;  // <-- Optional chaining\n\n      // Update field configuration\n      if (displayMode !== undefined) {  // <-- Skips if custom doesn't exist\n        panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayMode);\n        delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.displayMode;\n      }\n\n      // Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\n      if (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n        for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) {\n          for (let j = 0; j < (override.properties?.length || 0); j++) {\n            if (override.properties[j].id === 'custom.displayMode') {\n              // Override migration happens regardless of defaults.custom\n              override.properties[j].id = 'custom.cellOptions';\n              override.properties[j].value = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(overrideDisplayMode);\n            }\n          }\n        }\n      }\n    }\n    return panel;\n  });\n}\n```\n\nThe optional chaining `?.` on line 647 causes the entire defaults migration to be skipped if `custom` doesn't exist. While overrides migration (lines 659-668) runs independently, it creates an inconsistency: overrides reference `custom.cellOptions` but the defaults object may not have `custom` properly initialized.\n\n### Secondary Issue: Inconsistent Default Structure\n\n**PanelModel Default Definition** (`/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/PanelModel.ts`, lines 130-133):\n\n```typescript\nconst defaults: any = {\n  ...\n  fieldConfig: {\n    defaults: {},      // <-- No 'custom' object initialized\n    overrides: [],\n  },\n  ...\n};\n```\n\nThe default `fieldConfig` structure only initializes `defaults: {}` and `overrides: []`. There is **no `custom` object**. This means:\n\n1. Dashboards created before explicit `custom` properties were added won't have `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n2. Dashboards imported from external sources or created with minimal configuration structures won't have it\n3. The v38 migration assumes this structure will always exist, creating a silent failure\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Test Coverage Gap\n**File**: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`\n\nAll test cases (lines 9-445) have explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` defined. **Missing test case**: Dashboard with `fieldConfig` but without `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`.\n\nAll test inputs follow this pattern (lines 22-28):\n```go\n\"fieldConfig\": map[string]interface{}{\n    \"defaults\": map[string]interface{}{\n        \"custom\": map[string]interface{}{  // <-- Always present\n            \"displayMode\": \"basic\",\n        },\n    },\n    \"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n},\n```\n\n**No test covers**:\n```go\n\"fieldConfig\": map[string]interface{}{\n    \"defaults\": map[string]interface{}{\n        // No 'custom' property\n    },\n    \"overrides\": []interface{}{\n        map[string]interface{}{\n            \"properties\": []interface{}{\n                map[string]interface{}{\n                    \"id\":    \"custom.displayMode\",\n                    \"value\": \"gradient-gauge\",\n                },\n            },\n        },\n    },\n},\n```\n\n### Version Progression\n**File**: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v30.go` (lines 130-145)\n\nEarlier migrations (v30) handle missing `custom` by checking existence before access:\n\n```go\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n    if mappings, ok := defaults[\"mappings\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n        // Process mappings\n    }\n}\n```\n\nV30 doesn't assume `custom` exists and processes only fields that are present. **V38 breaks this pattern** by requiring `custom` to exist.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Backend Migration Pipeline\n- **Primary**: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go` (processPanelsV38, migrateOverrides, migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions)\n- **Impact**: Dashboard imports/saves via backend API, schema version advancement\n- **Scope**: All table panels in dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is not pre-initialized\n\n### Frontend Migration Pipeline\n- **Primary**: `/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts` (v38 conditional block, lines 644-674)\n- **Impact**: Dashboard viewing, panel rendering\n- **Scope**: Same as backend, compounded by inconsistency\n\n### Field Configuration Structure\n- **Primary**: `/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/PanelModel.ts` (default fieldConfig definition)\n- **Related**: `/workspace/public/app/plugins/panel/table/migrations.ts` (table panel migrations)\n- **Impact**: How field overrides are stored and serialized\n\n## Affected Schema Version\n- **Version**: 38 (Table cell display configuration migration: displayMode → cellOptions)\n- **Dashboard Versions**: Affects dashboards at schema version 37 (or earlier) that lack explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n- **Introduced**: Schema migration from v10.3 to v10.4\n- **Regression Type**: Silent data loss (field overrides not migrated)\n\n## Conditional Logic Failure\n\n### Failure Condition\nA dashboard triggers the regression when:\n\n1. **Panel type is 'table'** - Only table panels are processed by v38\n2. **Has fieldConfig** - Panel has field configuration structure\n3. **Has fieldConfig.defaults** - Defaults object exists\n4. **Missing fieldConfig.defaults.custom** - No explicit custom object (common in older/minimal dashboards)\n5. **Has fieldConfig.overrides with custom.displayMode** - Field-specific displayMode overrides exist\n\n### Why Dashboards With Explicit custom Are Unaffected\n\nWhen `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` IS explicitly defined:\n- Type assertion succeeds: `custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})` returns ok=true\n- Migration enters the processing block\n- Both defaults and overrides are correctly migrated\n- displayMode is converted to cellOptions and removed\n\n## Migration Chain\n\n```\nDashboard Schema v37 → V38 Migration → Schema v38\n    ↓                      ↓\nBackend Processes    Type assertion fails\n(if custom missing)   custom doesn't exist\n    ↓                  continue to next panel\nDatabase saved    Overrides not migrated\n    ↓\nFrontend loads       Optional chaining skips\nfrom database        defaults processing\n    ↓\nRenders with    Overrides may reference\nmissing formatting  non-existent custom.cellOptions\n```\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\nThe v38 migration must initialize `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` if it doesn't exist before processing:\n\n1. **Backend (v38.go)**: Initialize empty custom object if missing\n   ```go\n   custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\n   if !ok {\n       custom = make(map[string]interface{})\n       defaults[\"custom\"] = custom\n   }\n   // Now proceed with migration\n   ```\n\n2. **Frontend (DashboardMigrator.ts)**: Ensure custom object exists before assignment\n   ```typescript\n   if (!panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom) {\n       panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = {};\n   }\n   // Now safe to migrate\n   ```\n\n3. **Test Coverage**: Add test case for dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n\n4. **Consistency**: Review other migrations (v30, v35, v42) to ensure they follow the same pattern of initializing missing structures rather than skipping them\n\n### Prevention\n- All future schema migrations should validate/initialize required object structures before processing\n- Test coverage should include both \"structure exists\" and \"structure missing\" scenarios\n- Consider adding schema validation in the migration framework to catch these patterns
